# Repository File Inventory

## Purpose & Audience
This document catalogues every file in the Salt Marcher repository so contributors, reviewers, and maintainers can quickly audit assets, confirm file locations, and reference supporting materials during planning or review.

## Directory Map
| Path | Description | Primary Docs |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `.` | Root of the Salt Marcher repository. | [Root README](../README.md) |
| `salt-marcher/` | Source for the Salt Marcher plugin package, including build scripts and tests. | — |
| `todo/` | Planning notes and follow-up investigations for upcoming work. | [To-do index](../todo/README.md) |
| `wiki/` | Contributor-facing knowledge base for workflows and reference material. | [Wiki index](README.md) |
| `Notes/` | Historical meeting notes and review summaries for major features. | [Editor review notes](../Notes/cartographer-editor-review.md) |
| `References, do not delete!/` | Reference documents and mechanics archives required for compliance. | [Reference README](../References%2C%20do%20not%20delete%21/README.md) |

## Relevance Scale
Ratings reflect how strongly each file influences the user-facing features described across the wiki (Cartographer, Library, Encounter, UI, and supporting infrastructure).
- **10-9**: Core runtime assets required for the plugin to function in Obsidian (e.g. `src/`, `main.js`, `manifest.json`).
- **8-7**: Build inputs, primary source files, and configuration that directly shape behaviour (e.g. `package.json`, bundler/test configs).
- **6-5**: Quality gates, generated bundles, and ancillary assets that keep features reliable (`tests/`, lock files, compiled outputs).
- **4-3**: Documentation and supporting tooling with indirect impact.
- **2-1**: Third-party artefacts (e.g. vendored dependencies, external documentation) that do not materially affect behaviour beyond being present.

## Key Workflows
1. Consult the directory map above to understand how the repository is organised at a glance.
2. Use the comprehensive file listing below to locate specific assets, verify naming, or feed automation scripts. Relevance ratings follow the scale above: first-party runtime sources receive 9–10 scores, build/test scaffolding receives 5–8, and third-party dependency files are marked 1–2.
3. Refresh the inventory after structural changes by regenerating the list with `find ./salt-marcher -type f -print | sort` from the repository root and applying the same relevance heuristics.
